Oh ye, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last part of the knowledge of medicine together with its contents, and I have finished it through its explanations and by its declarations. And it has come to me in vision that I have completed it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and lost everywhere, so is the science destroyed and demolished, and nothing remains from it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that were moved by hands. And because of this has come the error and vanity, and the intentions have been closed and the science has been estranged.
Now it seems to me that I should revive it together with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come along with the forms of the cauteries' instruments and of the other tools of the craft with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, such as is necessary.
And because of this reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been estranged. And it is necessary for him who undertakes this to ascend in the knowledge of anatomy, as Galen says, as long as he knows the joints of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and tendons and the number of them, and their movements and restings, and from where their issue comes.
And because of this says Hippocrates that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little, and likewise in the art of hand.
And we tell you in the introduction of this book that who is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned, let him guard himself lest he err and deceive men; thus I have wanted many times to warn those who undertake this science but abandon their knowledge and experience.
For I have seen a foolish surgeon who cut, that is, an abscess or boil on the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries of the neck; why so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead in his hands.
And I have seen another surgeon who treated an old man's stone, and the stone was great; so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if it were cut out, he would die.
And I have seen another surgeon who took on the care of a duke from our land, who had a broken leg and with the break was wounded. And the ignorant surgeon bound the break over the wound with tight ligatures, and did not let it be washed at all, and thus left it like that for a long time; and he forbade anyone to untie them, and so remained until the leg became gangrenous and came to ruin.
I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come to loosen the leg; and when I loosened it, he was at peace and did not feel any pain.
But the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it, and the corruption did not cease to progress through the member until the entire limb was lost.
And I have seen another surgeon who burst an infected abscess, and then it inflamed because of the wickedness of his treatment.
For when a cancer is purged of melancholic humor, it does not agree to be touched with iron unless in such a place where one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the art of surgery is divided into two sections: one where there is danger in many situations; and I will show you in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Why it is necessary that you guard yourself so that the foolish surgeon may not speak ill of you.
Then take your arms in custody, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through God's grace you may come to salvation and be praised; and leave the frightful diseases with heavy sadness; and remove your arms from those who make you doubt, and have faith within yourself so that you can come from this world to the next one in glory.
Galen says in some of his warnings: "Do not undertake the care of a bad disease, unless you are called a foolish surgeon."
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapter is about cauterization with fire and medical cautery, and it is the chapter ordered from head to foot; and of the forms of instruments, and of cauterizing iron, and of all that is necessary in the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and venesection and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things; and it is the chapter that orders and describes the forms of instruments.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and fractures, and similar things; and it is ordered from head to foot, and describes the forms of instruments.
Therefore, so that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of each aid and the harm of each temperament.
I say that the quality of each aid and the harm is the longest word and most subtle science and secret response; and many of the wise have spoken about it and agreed with it; and I will shorten their words because I fear length.
I say that cauterization aids universally to all temperaments where there is matter, except for two temperaments: namely, the hot temperament with excess of matter, and the dry temperament with excess of matter.
In the hot and dry temperament with excess of matter, one group said that cauterization is a great aid, and the other group said the opposite, that cauterization is not useful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat or dryness, nor is it suitable for treating hot and dry diseases; and those who say the opposite claim that cauterization does great aid in treating hot and dry diseases that come into the bodies of men. For when you consider the body of man and its moisture compared to the temperament of fire, you find that the body is cold.
And I agree with this saying. For I have found it to be true by experience.
And in any case, do not interfere with it unless you are the one who has tried it and know by long experience the chapter of cauterization, and the diversity of temperaments of men, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the remedies and the time of application; for as to other complexions, we have no fear, especially in cold and moist diseases. And all the surgeons assembled and agreed on cauterization.
And know, son, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of treatments, and of greater goodness than medical cauterization.
For fire is simple, and does not affect any member except the one that is burned, and it does no harm to another member if its name is known.
The hot medicines come from one member to another, causing harm and bringing diseases of heavy sadness to the affected member, and perhaps killing the patient.
The fire, due to its simplicity and goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is excessiveness.
And I have found this by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of my words, because I do not like to deprive you of the secret which fire holds, and the quality of the work, how it heals diseases in bodies, as the philosophers say in demonstrating; take it into your thoughts.
And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauterizations should be done and chose specific hours.
And I say that cauterization is advisable in all times, because the remedies provided by cauterization are placed under, and especially when cauterizations are for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until a greater evil comes to the member.
And never think, dear son, as foolish surgeons do; for the disease that is healed by cauterization does not recur, and they say so themselves. But it's not like they believe, because cauterizations are not just a medicine that changes the temperament, but also dry up the humors that cause pain, and are more valuable than other medicines in terms of speed, effectiveness, and the virtue of their work and their treatment.
And it is a possible thing that the disease comes back once, according to the temperament of the patient and the place and virtue of the disease, and excesses are gathered in him from the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered at a place where there is little excess and moisture, such as for dens pain with cauterizations, and similar things, and that pain does not recur; but this happens rarely.
And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth trying after other treatments, but their intentions are false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer other modes of treatment for a disease and they do not work, then we administer the cauterization, and it works. Therefore, it is clear that cauterizations are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish surgeons.
The ancients said that cauterizations made with a golden instrument are more effective than those made with iron, and they did not say this only because of the quality of gold and its high substance; and they said that the place where the cauterization is made does not cause corruption, but this is not true for I have tried it and found that it is true in some men; and a golden cauterization is more effective than an iron one, as they said.
And in any case, when you heat an instrument made of gold, you cannot tell if it is hot enough by its color, and it cools down quickly; and if you heat it too much, it becomes damaged; and thus there are enough obstacles.
And therefore we use cauterizations made of iron that we have made suitable for our work.
Now I have arranged this chapter from head to foot, so that the way is more easy to find.
From cauterization of olive oil.
This cauterization is useful for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two types made by the cause of a disease called "soda", and by the cause of many humors that descend from the head to the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and pain in the temples and throat, and especially for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
The form of this cauterization is that the patient should be purged by a medicinal solution that cleanses the head three or four times, according to what virtue and age and custom of the patient can tolerate; and then reheat the patient's head.
And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on the scale; after putting the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and let where blood will come from it, then heat up the cauterization called "olivare", which is in this form:
And put it on the marked spot with ink, and make a descending and spreading motion with your hand little by little, turning it over; then lift up your hand suddenly, and reward the place if you see the bone 1 small inch deep; and if you don't see it, repeat the cauterization until you see the bone as I told you; after taking 1 piece of thread, put it in a warm wet cotton swab inside, and put it on the spot, and leave it for 3 days; then put on moistened cloth wrapped in a cloth; and leave it there until the heat is gone; then heal the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmacium" until it's healed.
And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; and for this reason, it is more helpful.
And some of them said that the cauterization should be done in such a way that part of the bone is burned, and then the burned part of the bone is to be removed and healed.
And the others say that the cauterization should be done so deeply that it reaches as far down into the bone as a thread that women put in their looms, and that the wound should be left open for a long time to let the humors drain out; then it should be cured and closed.
And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be entirely good in all cases, except perhaps for men who are already weak; and I think that I should leave it alone, because the nerves are weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other members; and similarly, if the patient's nerve is weak by nature, the initial effect of cauterization may be more salutary and less risky for me, and that is what I use to ensure a safe outcome.
From the ancient pain in the head.
When a chronic pain comes to the head and lasts for a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purges of the head and oils and plasters; and if one does the cauterization that we have just mentioned, it is not effective.
Take note if the nerve of the patient is strong and not too cold; then apply a cauterization under that one which we have mentioned above.
Then do the cauterization on each horn of the head right up to the bone, as we have said before, and do one cauterization in the place called "vasselz"; and it is a spot where you apply cupping glasses; and lift your hand so that you don't see right up to the bone: the patient feels a much greater pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary for the cauterizations on the horns to be more subtle than those done on the middle part of the head, and this is the form.
The cauterization of the head. When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and spreads to the eye, and the nerve is purged with cleansing medicines, and one has done the other treatments that I have said in the division of diseases, and none of these things are helpful: then one does cauterizations according to two methods, namely from medicine agar and iron.
The cauterization of medicine agar is that you take a stick of agar and remove its skin and re-coat it with 1 spoonful per two nerves, and then place the temple where the pain holds in such a way that you can re-place the agar stick under the skin; and when it has been placed, tie and tighten well and leave it thus for .xij. hours; and then untie it and treat it further with the agar paste, and let the wound be like this for 2 or 3 days; then put on a moistened cloth wrapped in a cloth until it is healed.
After that, heal with ointment until it is healed; and if you see fit to do the things of some purging medicines that I have written about or in the treatise on purging medicines.
The cauterization of iron is according to this manner. Heat the cauterizer in this form:
And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or has a small hollow in it, and on top there is a little appearance; and put it on the painful spot, hold your hand and turn the iron slightly, until half of the thickness of the copper is burned; and lift up your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is hidden, and decorates an abundance of blood.
After that, put cotton in a wet thread and put it on the spot for 3 days; then I put moistened cloth wrapped in a cloth, and then heal the spot with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cauterizer called "cultellare", all pointed, and beware of cutting the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
From migraine.
When you treat migraine as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cauterizations from medicine and iron do not work, then it is necessary to heat the cauterizer called "cultellare" until it is white; and then sign on the painful spot a line half a finger's length long, and withdraw your hand once, and tighten it so that you do not cut the artery and come close to the bone; and beware of the jawbone that moves when eating, and the nerves have regard for it, and spasms may come to the patient, and beware of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear and especially if one does not know what they are doing, and who is not experienced in this; and leave the work in my way. But I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it hurts in this book.
And if you see that these cauterizations do not suffice for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize at the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has two knives; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.

a single eyelash that points the eye At any time when the eyelashes are converted to stingers and point the eye, and it is done with a cauterization in two manners: that is to say by fire, or by burning medicine.
Or the fire cauterization orders the patient to let the eyelashes be as long and even as they are; and if they point at birth, then he must bind them so that they do not move until they have been born.
When they are born and are even, then the patient puts medicine in his eye; afterwards he places a mark on the parchment of the eye that is as like as a myrtle flower, and it is the beginning of the sign next to the eyelashes; then he puts moist cotton soaked in egg white and perfumed with persillium on the eye; then heat the cauterizer which is the form:

And if after this the eyelashes come and the parchment is softened then start again with the cauterization on that very same spot, as you did first; and if the lashes are protruding, then cauterize until the parchment is raised to its natural level, and is even, and do not point the lashes at the eye.
The cauterization with burning medicine is that you order the patient to let the lashes be as long and even as they are; then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and live coal, each one third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool down; then spread it on the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and put it on the eye parchment; and if the illness is in only one eye, then work with one, and if in both eyes also; and put cotton moistened with egg yolk under the eye; and the patient's eyelids should be in their natural state, and place your thumb showing on the medicine, and press once and lift up all the times that the patient feels a sting from the medicine, because it stings as much as fire. When you have done this for a long time, then take off the medicine with your thumb. And when the sting has passed, then lift off the medicine with your thumb and check if the parchment is raised as it would be if lifted by constraint of fire or incision; and if so, it's good. If not, then put more medicine on the spot where the medicine hasn't worked, until your work is even and your eyes are in order; then put moist cotton in butter until the burnt coal has cooled down; afterwards cure the spot with ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it's healed.

On the treatment of a fistula by cauterization
When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner.
Command the patient to place his head in your lap; then have him place his head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move or change position. Afterward put moist cotton soaked in egg white or persimmon juice over one eye, then heat the cautery which is thus formed: and shape it like the point of a feather quill, together with the handle; if you wish, make it pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, make it also like a tent; but nevertheless, what is shaped in this way will serve for your work.
After press the fistula if it is open, and take out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, then operate, and remove the boil. After put hot cauterized instrument on the area around the eye, holding your hand at a safe distance from the cautery to prevent accidents. Then place the heated cautery in the fatty part of the eye and corrupt it.
If you come to the bone at the beginning of the cautery, it would be good. But if not, then repeat the cautery one more time, and another time if necessary, and let it alone for 3 days. Then put on moist cotton in butter, and apply the unguent desiccative until it is healed, and if after 40 days it is still not healed, then apply corrosive astringent medicine until the bone is exposed; and treat according to what would come into his book (presumably a medical text or guide).
I must note that the following text describes a medieval surgical procedure that may not be considered safe or acceptable by modern medical standards. And they make it to the size of an egg; and hold your hand or cloth firmly, and do not let the patient move until the blister forms a scab; and it is necessary that someone places cotton moistened in eggs or in oil on the eye of the sick person. The blister soars up to the place of the fistula, and the pain passes through marvelous healing.
And if the fistula is healed through the cautery that we have said, it is good. If not, then it is necessary to administer potions at night, and bring the fistula back into its proper place in the body of the neck as is correct for its true location.

an abscess of the jaw
When an abscess comes to the root of the jaw or to the gum, or to the palate, or to the roots of the teeth, and after it has made pus and boils and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in sections, and it does not help: then it is necessary that you have a cauterization according to the size of the fistula. After that, boil or purify the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron rod comes up to the point of the fistula and to the last part; and do this once or twice, after that cure it as we have said in cures, until it is healed.
The movement of the teeth.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and it does not help, then put the patient's head in your healthy one; afterwards heat the cautery from which the form will come later in this way that you put a cloth on the tooth; and put hot hastanment inside the cautery and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and repeat the cautery according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let it sit for an hour and a rich foul breath.
And in this way the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the gums softened are restrained, and the moisture corrupted is dried.
of the pain of the teeth
When pain of the teeth comes from cold or there is cold or wetness, and medical remedies do not help, then it is necessary to have a cautery in two manners: and a cautery of butter and a cautery of fire.
Cautery of butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and dip the end in an iron or silver spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a thimble, and soak it in melted butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold until it cools down; and do so often until its virtues reach the root of the tooth. And if you see that the wool and cotton are soaked in cold butter, and put them on the sore tooth, and place a hot iron so that the fire comes to the gum of the tooth.
The cautery with fire is such that you take an iron or silver cauterizer, and make it thick so that the fire doesn't reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery until the form comes out later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down. Do this often, for the pain will be gone that same day or the next. And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in the heating of that cautery, and then let it cool off; and this is the form of the cautery:
When scrofulas are of a watery and cold moistness, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery so that it takes this form, and have two openings for the vapors to come out from the other side; and place the heated cautery once or twice on the abscess as much as is necessary until the point of the abscess comes to a head; and if the abscess is small, then use a cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it in for three days; and put on moistened cotton wool in butter until the swelling is gone; after that, cure the place with ointments and liniments until it is healed.

of the plague cautery
The ancients said that at the plague one should make cauterizations with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia as thick and as long as your thumb; and let it be dry, and moisten it with oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize 1 cautery between the shoulder blades and the neck, and 2 small cauterizations a little below in the part which is under the beard; and 2 cauterizations between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining backwards by a little; and 1 cautery in the breast, and another on the stomach, and 1 between the two shoulder blades, and 2 on the sides of the breast behind the cautery that is between the two shoulder blades; and do not press your hand, but make it open as when smelling.
And the ancient said that no man should use a cautery of fire similar to a razor, and heat it up and put it between the ribs, until it comes into contact with the aposteme; and suddenly the pain goes away, as we have said in the case of the liver aposteme. But in this work there is fear for the sick person's death now, or a fistula will come which cannot be healed.
of the mumps
When you cure the disease of the mumps in the way that we have said in the sections on treatments, and it does not benefit, then I add three manners of cauterization, which are all good.
Of which one manner is that you make 3 cauterizations, or 4, along the length of the swelling, according to the figure of the liver cautery that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all of the cautery, and the sick person be lying on their back.
And another manner of cauterization is that you heat the cautery which has 2 handles, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and raise the key which is near the swelling, or where the sick person's ribs come towards their left side, and be the elevation from which you raise the key according to the shape of the body, according to its length, and the cautery be along the width of the chest.
Afterwards, you put the two handles into the fire so that the key is scorched from the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four of them. And if you wish, then cauterize the entire cautery with three handles. Afterwards, cure the sick person when it has gotten a good burn for a long time, and this is as effective as the other cures mentioned before.

Cauterization is not effective for dropsy, except for the manner called "asclytes". Afterwards, leave the cauterizations to ooze and get a good burn for a long time, and do not neglect the sick person's treatment after the cauterization; and healing will hasten, and both intentions (i.e., the physical and spiritual aspects of health) will be restored together with God's help.

of the treatment of hemorrhoids (emorroides)
When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and made of thick, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and they have been treated as we said in divisions, and it has not benefited, then make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that which is completely behind the navel, a little to the side and a little triangularly, and one cautery under the navel, two fingers apart.

of old pain in any member When pain comes in any member, from falling or striking, and this pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and virtue and its location of twists and pain. of wound-making (or surgery)
Wounds are helped by cautery in some cases with great effect, and especially the illnesses that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. swelling up

Of the remedies
When the disease that is called "albaras" is inflamed, and the art of medicine does not help anything, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the best sulfur, until the scab is removed and its color changed; then cure it with flour of chickpeas and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of cockle and blood of almond, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and keep it in place until it heals.
the cure for syphilis by cauterization
When the chancre comes at the beginning, and you want to stop it from spreading, if you cauterize it with a cautery in the shape of a circle, all around the edge of the chancre. And some wise men said that we should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen before; and a more direct thing is to cauterize around it, with the cautery that is called "circle", as we have said about many other cauterizations.

the cure by fire with iron
Another manner of disease called "corrodens" which is nothing other than a gangrenous member, for it destroys the members just like fire does to dry wood. the cure of trembling.

the boils or buboes.

when the artery is cut Often there are great hemorrhages of blood from the artery that is cut in the wound that appears first, or at the incision of the apostema, or at the cauterization of the member, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
And yet whenever this happens to someone, if you hurry and put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and strain it hard until the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more blood comes out; then set on fire several small and large olive-shaped cauterizers as many as they are red; then grasp one, either great or small according to the wound and the place in which the artery runs, and put the cauterizer on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cauterizer so long until the blood is stemmed.
And if the blood spurts out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauterizer is extinguished, then take hastily another one of the cauterizers that are on fire.
And do not stop doing this one after the other until the blood is stemmed; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when blood pours from an artery, it cannot be well stemmed on its own when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not closed off, or by tightly tying a thread, or by applying medicines which have the power to stem blood; and let it be tied and strained in good time.

Quant li dent lochent (When the teeth decay)

There are many similarities of abscesses according to what remembrance comes later from one and the other in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and in surgery; and there are two manners in which one is similar itself, and due to moisture. And the second manner is for the places where it is at the body. For the abscesses of the head are different than those of the fundament, and the abscesses of the hollowed place are different than those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in work.
And there are abscesses which should not be pierced until the body is dead according to its completion; and there are those of such that it is necessary to pierce them when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, such as an abscess that comes near joints. For when an abscess comes near joints, and one leaves it until it is putrid around it, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be corrupted, because of which there is a contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is near the principal limb, and you delay the perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; or it is near the fundament, so that when one pierces it while it is dead; and it should not be pierced with an unripe digestion completed, except for that which is near the fundament, lest it become putrid inside and become a fistula; and cannot heal in a long term.

Translation:
And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must proceed before treatments of abscesses, and see below the chapter.
Abscesses
Or wounds of the head come from small abscesses, and are manners of being in a boil, as also the sore of a hen, and there are many likenesses. There are those that are fat and like pustules; and some such that are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt that they will become contrary. And the operation of cutting them is this: first try with one instrument which is called "entromissoire", from whose form comes what it contains. For if it contains moisture, then make a hole above the long part. And when the moisture has been emptied, then scrape off without leaving any of the peel that contained the moisture, for it will return again if anything is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian balm, if it is present; if not, in water and soap, and fill the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain from the night will have passed. And then reinsert the cotton as before, on the second day, and the third, so that you know well that there is no longer any of the night remaining; then cure the wound with ointment according to what is convenient, until it is sound. The ancient ones spoke and said about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land anyone who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
For those who have suffocated, it is necessary that the incision of the throat which is called "epiglote" be cut out; and this is not done by others, because all the veins and the pulse of the patient are warm near the abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the armpits. and they should be so convenient to the cutting of the epiglote that there is no flesh and the veins are long enough in length.

and leave the wound open for a piece. (This implies allowing the wound to heal on its own without stitches or further closure)

and so the ancient ones command to leave the wound open as long as the badness of the illness has not passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal it, until it was healed.
and I will tell you what I have seen. I saw a young lady take 1 dagger, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the womb;
and I was called to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
I uncovered the wound and found blood issuing from it, and I knew that she had not cut too close to the vein nor cut deeply enough into the throat, and the veins were issuing forth through the wound.
I rushed, sewed up the wound, and healed her until she was whole again.
and it came to pass with the young lady that she had no further harm than being hoarse in her voice, and after that she returned to her usual state.
Therefore I say that there is not much fear in cutting into the epiglottis. (Note: This is a conclusion drawn from the story, suggesting that while the procedure may seem drastic, it can be effective and have a relatively good outcome)

and I will tell you about an abscess that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take it as an example and have guidance in your work.
He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from an internal cause within the body,

Of the pain that comes from windiness This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen those things that I am telling you.
I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the upper arm;
and little by little, I saw it rise up like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, just like bright silver when it runs from one place to another;

then she told me that it was twisting around the body, just as I had seen it.
I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen that disease behave in this manner before. However, I had often seen well-known physicians allow the pain to move from place to place; but I had never seen it happen as I did see in that woman.
and I thought that it was because the woman had a weak body and the veins were uncovered, and therefore that windiness appeared constrained.

Of arrows
The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they lodge.
The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small, and hairy, and tied on; and of those with two edges, and those with claws, and of those that have fragments or splinters. and the one that lodges in any member does so in two ways: either it lodges in the main member, or it is lodged under the ligament;
such as brain, liver, spleen, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members. When it lodges in any of these places, and the sign of death, which I will tell you next, becomes apparent: so be warned to beware of extracting this arrow, for death follows afterwards in various forms. and if you do not see that bad sign, and the arrow is not deeply lodged, then pull it out, and heal the wound.
And the sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces it and lodges in the skull, and you see a piece of flesh flying forward that is above the brain. is a sudden and great darkness, and a deep sleep, and vertigo, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting of bile. and perchance it happens without pain in the nostrils or ears; and perchance it causes loss of speech and voice. and from the wound there comes out a moist white discharge, like pus, and also as black as charcoal.
and if you see this sign, then be on guard for the cure, and pull out the arrow if it is not already gone.
The signs of the spleen when it is pierced by the arrow are that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty. and perhaps the spleen becomes swollen like pus, and flows with black blood, and there is coldness and cold sweat, and syncope. then you should be certain without doubt that death will ensue.
And the signs of the arrow that never lodges in the navel are: there is a foaming discharge coming out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and sighs loudly and asks for cold air.
And if the arrow lodges in the covering of the liver, it is located near the small ribs; and there is a great pain and a great agony, and the sick person sighs; and the muscles of all the members of the shoulders are convulsed.
And if the arrow lodges in the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat comes out of the wound.
And if the arrow lodges in the abdomen and there is no passing of feces through the rectum, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
And if the arrow lodges in the bladder, and urine comes out and flows away, and the sick person feels a great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
The other members, such as the face, arms, neck, shoulders, and armpits, and the spine of the back, and the ribs, and the hips, and the thighs, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions. Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
When dislocation comes to anyone, then it must be returned to its proper place immediately.
For if you delay, the swelling will increase, and by chance if it is set back in place with force, then it should not be moved to its proper place until it has deflated: it causes many pains and other sufferings.
In any case, when this happens, you should heal the patient first, then let him rest until the swelling has subsided; then apply warm water and oil to the limb, gently clean it, and treat each member so that each joint comes back into its place.
And I have ordained the chapters on dislocations up until this point.
of the jaws

When the dislocation is small, it will return to its place by itself within a few days.

and in this way the servants should hold the patient's head, and insert a mirror on a stick into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if it is two-thirds deep; and with one hand, place it in the middle, and with the other two hands be outside to balance it; and command the patient to relax his jaws and move them in all directions.
And the mirror should be placed in a straight line with it, until it returns to its place.
And if it is difficult to return them to place, or if they are both jaws together, then warm water and oil should be applied to them, until they are lightly cleaned; and do not delay the return, as we have said.

and then he may take what he wants lightly, and not strain himself to open his mouth to eat and drink, until the jaws have completely healed and are sound.

And when you see this, then know that it is a perilous condition; and many times death comes to the person who experiences it within eight days.

of the shoulder joint dislocation

So then you should probe into it, until you are certain, and once you are sure, then start the treatment.
And it is known that a dislocation occurs when the shoulder goes downwards towards the collarbone, and you will find a clear distinction between the healthy and diseased shoulders, and you will see a manifest difference. and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and under the collarbone, at the point where the arm meets the body, just like an empty nest; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their side, nor make any movement.
and also, if it is dislocated upwards, then it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly at the point where the arm meets the body.
and this way of dislocating is not to be reduced (i.e. restored to its original position) when it is new or if the child is ill.
And the method is that the minister raises the patient's hand up high, then places their fingers under the collarbone, and raises the jointure with force upwards to its place; and the minister raises the hand and extends it upwards, then places it back down, and it will come back quickly.
And if it doesn't come back as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the minister should gently and soothingly apply a compress, such as a decoction of alecost, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and bring it to the place.
and then the patient should be covered on their back, and a strip of linen of equal thickness, not too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the collarbone; then the minister should place their elbow on top of the strip, and gently lift the head of the shoulder, and pull the patient's hand.
and another minister should grasp the patient's head, so that it does not move down; and the shoulder will come back immediately, and if you see that it is restored to its place in this way, then know.
and it is that you should have a man present who is larger than the patient, and stand with their shoulder against the patient's back, and push the collarbone up high, so that the patient hangs from the arm. and another minister should pull the patient's hand downwards towards their belly. And if the patient is too lightweight, they can hang something heavy with them, and the dislocation will return immediately.
And it is also healed in another way: and that is by sticking a long spit into the ground, whose end is as thick as a fist, and not too big or too thin. and then it is placed under the patient, but in such a way that it is covered with a soft cloth on top, and the patient's hand is stretched out to the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
and if it does not return after all the things we have said, then do this cure: take a spit of two arm-lengths and three fingers' width in diameter, which has the end rounded so that it can easily enter into depth under the collarbone, according to this shape.
and tie a cloth on top of the spit so that it does not hurt the patient, then place it under the patient's collarbone; and stretch out your arm over the long spit, and tie the elbow to the spit, and the arm at the hand, then put the arm on a cushion of a wooden board, one finger's width thick, and have the hands hanging down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will come back immediately.
And once it is healed, in whatever way it may be, then you should place under the collarbone a ball of wool of equal thickness; and apply an ointment made from flour powder with incense and egg yolks all over the shoulder and around it; and bind the bandage under the collarbone gently, and turn the cloth back on the ointment, and wrap the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
And it is necessary that he rest a little while, until the members are comforted, because it will heal more quickly; and then let him rest some more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
And if the joint is out of place because it has been moistened or for some other reason, then you should apply cauteries to three punctures, such as those used on the front or back of a cautery stick.
And if you do all this and the dislocation happens again after seven days, and the joint does not hold and the arm cannot be lifted upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
The dislocation that occurs towards the chest or breasts or back is caused by a blow or stretching of the hands, and it requires another type of treatment. And one must treat it until it is healed.
And if after healing comes swelling in the member and slow movement, then the patient should bathe many times until the swelling is alleviated and the member returns to its original state.
of the shoulder dislocation.
Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated in various ways and returns to its place in the same way, whether it was dislocated in front or behind, and the dislocation is not restored, because one can see it well and feel it well; and dislocates according to each figure. And when you join the diseased shoulder to the healthy one, it will be quite apparent. Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor can it touch its own shoulder in any way.
And it is necessary to treat it so that hot abscesses do not form, because if hot abscesses do form, it will be painful to reduce it; and by chance it cannot be completely reduced, especially when it occurs in the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance death can occur.
And the restoration is this: when it can be reduced to such an extent that one can bring it back into place, then you should extend its hand with both of yours; and its arms should be spread out, and the hands of the minister should follow the shoulder around, on top and underneath, and push the joint into its hollow or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
And if the dislocation is in front, it will come back when it doubles its hand over its own hand, and presses the root of the palm against the shoulder that was dislocated.
And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension; and have two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with both of their hands, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm from each side, and while you are wrapping a double long and wide cloth around it.
and when the minister has joined the joint to their hand, they should anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, and then push the joint firmly until it returns.
and when it is back in its place, then apply a dry ointment with egg yolk on top of the joint, and bind it firmly, and let the arm rest against the patient's neck for some days, and then release it.
And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the bandage and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the ointment and the bandage, and let it be thus for some days, until it is firmly set, and then release it.
And if it feels swollen after the joint has been put back in place, and it stiffens, then bathe it and rub it gently, and press on it until it is soothed; or you can apply a poultice made from fat sheep's wool to the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and let it go into a bath. and when it sweats, then rub the joint gently, then put the poultice back on, and then go into a bath; and do this twice or three times, until it is healed; and if you see fit, apply a compress made from moistened cow's hair that has been heated with butter, and bind it to the joint, and it will return to its normal state.
the dislocation of the hand.
The joint of the hand is dislocated and it is a light return, more than other joints. Nevertheless, it is necessary to bring it back into place quickly, even if it is swollen or if a hot abscess forms in it.
And the reduction is that you place the diseased hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and the minister should place it evenly, so that his palm is over the appearance of the joint, and push it back into place until it returns.
However, it is necessary to check if it is properly in place; then have the patient place their back of hand on a table at extension and reduction. And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then have the patient place their back of hand on a table, and the minister should put their hand over the appearance of the joint. If it returns now, it's good.
If not, then apply a soothing plaster to the abscess and let it be so without reattempting the reduction.
And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after any number of days, then the joint remains twisted.
and it does no harm to the patient until such time as the hand is softened and cannot grasp anything: then know that the nerves are cut or the arteries are damaged; if there is no other reason for this than to use a cautery near the case, and by chance it is not worth anything else.
And when the hand is back in place, then apply the ointment that we have said, and bind it and let it be for five days, then release it and let it be thus.
And if he cannot move it well and there is some swelling, then bathe the hand in warm water, and rub it gently until it is healed.
of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
At any time, the fingers of the hand can become dislocated on either side, or towards the back of the palm or towards the belly.
Then extend the finger and push the dislocation back into place with your fingers, then hold the tip of the finger and gently bend it towards the joint.
and let it be for two days, and then put it back in its place that day; and do not bind it, as we have said, and release it every day, and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this often, until it is straight.
and do the same thing if it is dislocated towards the belly of the hand, and do what you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same thing when it is dislocated from the other side.
of the dislocation of the hip bone (ischium) at the back.
When the hip bone (ischium) at the back or near the tailbone is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, because death quickly follows the patient.
And the signs are that the patient's bowels jump out without volition, and they cannot be held in, and multiple members become softened, such as the two thighs or both arms or one.
And many times the hip bone moves to four parts; that which moves at the back is called "giltbiositez".
The treatment is to reduce it, if the giltbiositez has come since childhood; if not, there will be no cure or healing at all.
